## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models population growth rate dP/dt as a function of population size P and time t, which is the central problem in population dynamics. Classical models range from simple exponential growth to density-dependent models with possible time-varying parameters.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent growth)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (growth rate decreasing logarithmically with population)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Strong Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population threshold)
- Weak Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 + P) (reduced growth at low density without extinction threshold)
- Logistic with harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (logistic growth with proportional removal)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (rational density dependence)
- Time-varying logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (seasonal carrying capacity or growth rate)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible sigmoidal growth)
- Von Bertalanffy type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance)
- Polynomial density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (cubic population dynamics)
- Exponential with time decay: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (time-dependent intrinsic growth rate)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional-order density dependence)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density dependence (negative feedback) → Terms like P*(1 - c*P) or P*log(c/P) indicating growth suppression at high density
- Allee effects (positive density dependence at low P) → Cubic terms in P such as P*(P-c1)*(c2-P) or quadratic multipliers
- Carrying capacity structure → Growth rate equals zero at a specific P value, creating equilibrium via factored polynomial in P
- Seasonal/periodic forcing → Multiplicative sinusoidal modulation sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) on growth parameters
- Metabolic scaling → Power-law terms P**c with fractional exponents reflecting allometric biological scaling (e.g., 3/4 power law)
- Compensatory vs depensatory mortality → Whether per-capita rate dP_dt/P is monotonically decreasing (compensatory) or has a hump (depensatory) in P
- Immigration/constant influx → Additive constant term independent of P, representing external population input
- Ratio of polynomials in P → Rational functions P/(1+c*P) indicating resource competition with handling time or interference

## Analysis

The GT expression is:
$$f(t,P) = 0.877 \cdot P \cdot \sin(0.567t) + 0.701 \cdot (1 - P/65.75) \cdot P$$

Expanding:
$$f(t,P) = 0.877 \cdot P \cdot \sin(0.567t) + 0.701 \cdot P - 0.01066 \cdot P^2$$

This has the form: $P^2 \cdot a + P \cdot b + P \cdot \sin(ct)$ where the sin term has no phase shift (or equivalently, phase shift = 0).

Let me check the candidates systematically.

**Candidate 27**: $P^2 c_0 \cos(c_1 t + c_2) + P c_3 \sin(c_4 t + c_5) + P c_6 + c_7$

Setting $c_0 = 0$ (eliminating the cos term), $c_7 = 0$:
$$P c_3 \sin(c_4 t + c_5) + P c_6$$

Set $c_3 = 0.877$, $c_4 = 0.567$, $c_5 = 0$, $c_6 = 0.701$. This gives:
$$0.877 P \sin(0.567t) + 0.701 P$$

But we're missing the $-0.01066 P^2$ term. We can use the $P^2 c_0 \cos(c_1 t + c_2)$ term — but that has a $\cos$ with time dependence. Setting $c_1 = 0$: $P^2 c_0 \cos(c_2)$, which is just $P^2 \cdot \text{const}$. 

So set $c_1 = 0$, $c_0 \cos(c_2) = -0.01066$. For example, $c_2 = 0$, $c_0 = -0.01066$.

Then candidate 27 becomes:
$$-0.01066 P^2 + 0.877 P \sin(0.567t) + 0.701 P + 0 = \text{GT}$$

**This matches the GT exactly!**

**Verification**: GT = $0.877 P \sin(0.567t) + 0.701P - 0.01066P^2$

Candidate 27 with $c_0 = -0.01066$, $c_1 = 0$, $c_2 = 0$, $c_3 = 0.877$, $c_4 = 0.567$, $c_5 = 0$, $c_6 = 0.701$, $c_7 = 0$:
$$(-0.01066)P^2 \cos(0) + 0.877 P \sin(0.567t) + 0.701P + 0 = -0.01066P^2 + 0.877P\sin(0.567t) + 0.701P$$

This is identical to the GT. ✓

Several other candidates also match (e.g., candidates 3, 6, 23, 24, 41, 43, and others that contain $P^2$, $P$, and $P\sin(ct)$ or $P\cos(ct)$ terms with enough flexibility), but candidate **27** is the clearest match.
